  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_c36358ab-b314-4988-ba63-8aebabf5b8fe'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();

              <span id="reviewTextContainer428661262" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14213588318189586626">very ordinary story like all the common stories in our Egyptian Drama, it shows the hero of the story as a so freaking smart such that he can beat all his enemies and the enemies of the county who are, as usual, corrupted, frankly, nothing is new about this book that will urge me to read for the same writer again.<br/><br/>beside, the way, the writer took the Muslims picture with, is the same way that we always see in our movies and series nowadays, he shed light only on the narrow minded people who belon</span>
  <span id="freeText14213588318189586626" style="display:none">very ordinary story like all the common stories in our Egyptian Drama, it shows the hero of the story as a so freaking smart such that he can beat all his enemies and the enemies of the county who are, as usual, corrupted, frankly, nothing is new about this book that will urge me to read for the same writer again.<br /><br />beside, the way, the writer took the Muslims picture with, is the same way that we always see in our movies and series nowadays, he shed light only on the narrow minded people who belong to Islam and showed them in a very bad figure while at the same time shows the behaviour of the hero who is working in a night club and some of the people who are working there in a way that makes the reader feel pity for their conditions although it is clear for everyone that their work is wrong. the same message is transmitted over and over the same way in trial to change the Conservative Islamic culture of the people in this country.<br /><br />Although, the writer has a very good talent in drawing the sense but I did not like his thought which represents his ideology representing it as the normal way of thinking and any other ideology is somehow wrong.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2576008329" />
    <a title="Jalilah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4656570-jalilah"><img alt="Jalilah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577750741p2/4656570.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2576008329?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jalilah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jalilah" href="/user/show/4656570-jalilah">Jalilah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9789992142660" href="/book/show/11309964-vertigo">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4656570-jalilah?shelf=mena-2018-challenge">mena-2018-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4656570-jalilah?shelf=middle-east-north-africa">middle-east-north-africa</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4656570-jalilah?shelf=thriller-mystery">thriller-mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2576008329" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8763452432192641297">Because Political thrillers are not the kind of genre I usually read, I'm surprised I ended up liking this book as much as I did. The many different characters with long detailed histories was confusing and made it hard to get into, as well as the fact that there are almost all male characters, however once I got into the story it became quite compelling. <br/> This book is about corruption in Egypt, so of course is very relevant. The author actually worked for the former president Mubarak and has an</span>
  <span id="freeText8763452432192641297" style="display:none">Because Political thrillers are not the kind of genre I usually read, I'm surprised I ended up liking this book as much as I did. The many different characters with long detailed histories was confusing and made it hard to get into, as well as the fact that there are almost all male characters, however once I got into the story it became quite compelling. <br /> This book is about corruption in Egypt, so of course is very relevant. The author actually worked for the former president Mubarak and has an insider view of what goes on with the rich and powerful in his country. It's also a story of the innocent little guy against the evil, powerful giant, the "giant" being the powerful businessmen, corrupt politicians and all those who associate with them including the famous entertainers. My main critique is the few and stereotypical female characters in the book. <br />There is Ghada the "good girl", Aya the protagonists weak sister who marries a fundamentalist and Sally, the dancer who, no surprise here for anyone who is aware of the status of dancers in the Middle East, is a greedy, scheming prostitute. For people in the know she seems to be modelled after a real life dancer named Dina. Unfortunately Mourad's depiction is based more on how society views professional dancers rather than actual facts, so it's disappointing on that level.<br />All and all however it's an interesting read that I'd recommend to people interested in Egypt and its recent history. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8763452432192641297" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2996832689" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2996832689" />
    <a title="Bobbi Steele" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39858798-bobbi-steele"><img alt="Bobbi Steele" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570580736p2/39858798.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2996832689?book_show_action=true">Oct 18, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bobbi Steele" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bobbi Steele" href="/user/show/39858798-bobbi-steele">Bobbi Steele</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9789992142660" href="/book/show/11309964-vertigo">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2996832689" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17900035569482468641">Vertigo is a political book that plays on the corrupt power structures of egyptian society by placing them on figures that are slightly removed from a directly political environment. <br/><br/>The novel follows the story of Achmed (I read the German version, so the names might be slightly different), who tries to make a societal difference. What this difference is becomes the main plot of the novel that might remind the readers of the Arab Spring movements. It’s a step towards a country no longer ruled by</span>
  <span id="freeText17900035569482468641" style="display:none">Vertigo is a political book that plays on the corrupt power structures of egyptian society by placing them on figures that are slightly removed from a directly political environment. <br /><br />The novel follows the story of Achmed (I read the German version, so the names might be slightly different), who tries to make a societal difference. What this difference is becomes the main plot of the novel that might remind the readers of the Arab Spring movements. It’s a step towards a country no longer ruled by dictators. <br /><br />In the German translation, at least, the city feels foreign and the westernised city of Cairo is mixed with the still strongly Egyptian city that is shown in mini plots throughout the novel. These mini plots, as foreign as they feel, allow the reader to experience several sides of Egyptian society that may not otherwise be accessible like religious superstition with pictures, demons taking over people’s bodies, shisha cafes, marriage, shame and differences in gender/ romantic relationships. <br /><br />I read the book to better understand a culture I’m in contact with on a daily basis through friends and family, but have never experienced firsthand since the political situation is so unstable. Some of the plots that took place in the book were too cliche for me, or even the way women were courted was a little too foreign and made me feel uncomfortable. It’s hard to imagine a society where women are seen as weak, superstitious and dependant on everything — including calling a cab to go home. <br /><br />Overall, I don’t think I’ll read another book by this author, but it does open a lot of questions that I now have for Egypt and its future. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17900035569482468641" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Unfortunaly, there are a lot of typos in the novel which should have been caught and corrected in revision.<br/><br/>As for the content of the novel, I believe the characters are very real ... there are quite some characters you can totally relate to a real-life person in a way that makes writers always claim that </span>
  <span id="freeText8855891060381617745" style="display:none">Not bad at all for a first novel. I think we can expect more mature trials from this tallented writer in the near future. His writing style is kinda funny although it sometimes lacks structure. Unfortunaly, there are a lot of typos in the novel which should have been caught and corrected in revision.<br /><br />As for the content of the novel, I believe the characters are very real ... there are quite some characters you can totally relate to a real-life person in a way that makes writers always claim that "ay tashaboh bain sha7'seyyat el-rewaya wel-waqe3 howa ma7d sodfa.. wel-7ede2 yefham" :)<br />The end of the novel, although very well written and not rushed, turned out to be not very realistic and a bit childish ... I mean law heyya dih nehayet el-fasad makansh 7add 3'olob :-)))<br /><br />But overall its a respect-worthy attempt to discuss some pretty complicated issues in a very human context.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17301566973274553229">The best thing about this book is that the author was able to portray all the corruption of Egypt in a novel written in 2007, predicting all the circumstances that made the 2011 revolution explode. Ahmed Morad's realism made me feel I am a part of the story, longing to have a new revolution again. Like Ahmed Kamel we should fight, we should try to erase all the corruption we are surrounded by, even if in an anonymous way, like the way his revolt was made. Chapeau Ahmed Morad</span>

          </span>
        </div>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Ahmad Gamal</span></div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer660299394" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6644828074315032293">I believe I am not the best to provide a review for novels -as I am not that much into them-, specially Arabic ones. However, I feel the urge to write one for this novel as:<br/><br/>It is one of the best novels I have ever read, in Arabic at least. I find it better than his latest: "الفيل الأزرق". That does not necessarily mean that it is not good, however, I like the Politics and social corruption reflected in this one. Or maybe just because I could feel that I am part of it.<br/><br/>Ahmad's refusal to give in t</span>
  <span id="freeText6644828074315032293" style="display:none">I believe I am not the best to provide a review for novels -as I am not that much into them-, specially Arabic ones. However, I feel the urge to write one for this novel as:<br /><br />It is one of the best novels I have ever read, in Arabic at least. I find it better than his latest: "الفيل الأزرق". That does not necessarily mean that it is not good, however, I like the Politics and social corruption reflected in this one. Or maybe just because I could feel that I am part of it.<br /><br />Ahmad's refusal to give in to humiliation and his decision to give up his job for his dignity. Alaa's utopia, his sense of perfect morality and refusal to go with the flow. And Gouda, who is viewed at the very beginning as a flat character but then comes to prove that he is more than he seems to be.<br /><br />The author's style is, as usual, both amusing and exciting. It got me emotionally engaged with the novel, that I could feel my heart beating faster. He successfully was able to get me to actually live every moment of the novel, especially through his perfect description of almost every single detail, that I could actually see whatever he is describing.<br /><br />The ending was shocking, at least I found it so. The way the incidents develop guided my expectations to a totally different type of ending, and thus it came to shock me.<br /><br />Yet I did not like how trivial and shallow, the female Ayah was viewed. It was as if the incidents controlled her, not the other way around, unlike Sally, who seemed to take advantage of whatever obstacles she stumbles upon. Even when she decided to change, the way it was written / described was not as strong as the way her first change was described.<br /><br />However, over all, I believe this novel could be one of the best novels I have read, specially when it comes to the political, religious and social corruption significance, which could be very well related to the current Egyptian reality.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6644828074315032293" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/452607049" />
    <a title="Mostafa Elshaier" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13953479-mostafa-elshaier"><img alt="Mostafa Elshaier" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1352140703p2/13953479.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/452607049?book_show_action=true">Nov 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mostafa Elshaier" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mostafa Elshaier" href="/user/show/13953479-mostafa-elshaier">Mostafa Elshaier</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer452607049" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15551399478661923483">It's really hard to find an author who writes about society's problems, standards and political corruption without boring you to death, especially when the reader is part of that society and knows/lives what is happening around him. But, Ahmad Mourad's Vertigo is an exception. Vertigo takes the society's double standards and old regime's corruption to a whole 'other level. Mourad's perspective and way of looking and analyzing the pre-Jan25 Egypt deserves a look at. He really knows how to tell a </span>
  <span id="freeText15551399478661923483" style="display:none">It's really hard to find an author who writes about society's problems, standards and political corruption without boring you to death, especially when the reader is part of that society and knows/lives what is happening around him. But, Ahmad Mourad's Vertigo is an exception. Vertigo takes the society's double standards and old regime's corruption to a whole 'other level. Mourad's perspective and way of looking and analyzing the pre-Jan25 Egypt deserves a look at. He really knows how to tell a story.<br /><br />Highlight of the book: Despite the fact that Vertigo's core is political, Mourad didn't forget to shed a light on the romantic part in the story, and it was simple yet enjoyable.<br /><br />The downside: Mourad sometimes loses himself in detailing each character in the book (even the ones who didn't make a big effect in the story telling)And these details, are sometimes, distracting.<br /><br />4.5/5</span>
  <a data-text-id="15551399478661923483" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6834378629097133395">Ahmed Mourad is a talented writer. It’s about a young photographer who witness the death of his friend who happens to be in the right place at the wrong time. The only flaw in the story is the us</span>
  <span id="freeText6834378629097133395" style="display:none">Ahmed Mourad is a talented writer. I read all of his books and fell in love with each and everyone of them except for the last 2. <br />Vertigo is a crime thriller. It’s about a young photographer who witness the death of his friend who happens to be in the right place at the wrong time. He vows to find the killer and avenge the death of his best friend. <br />Mourad has a way of making his characters so vivid and real and that’s due to his obsession with minute details. The only flaw in the story is the usage of real life events and characters (names were changed) to create his plot. It was like reading the tabloids and listening to all the juicy gossips. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6834378629097133395" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('n5+FSllAOYUV51G1jrhCf6eokpZJEkwsOJqYmM6wjjD8mNnvCZSb6ZK2usQkQ3cywwIq9ZRAZHvZpaKdo7Q2ug==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('3jXaJTevmAKtcuv5aufPF3wamcXO1Va12diqqAsNXLu9MoaAZ3s6biojAIjAHPpaGLAhphOHfuI455CtZgnkMQ==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/1633682._">About أحمد مراد</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer3078446801270003321">أحمد مراد.. <br/>كاتب مصري من مواليد القاهرة 1978، تخرّج في مدرسة ليسيه الحرّية بباب اللوق عام 2006 قبل أن يلتحق بالمعهد العالي للسينما ليدرس التصوير السينمائي، وتخرّج عام 2001 بترتيب الأول على القسم، ونالت أفلام تخرّجه "الهائمون - الثلاث ورقات - وفي اليوم السابع" جوائز للأفلام القصيرة في مهرجانات بإنجلترا وفرنسا وأوكرانيا.. <br/>بدأ أحمد كتابة روايته الأولي "فيرتيجو" في شتاء عام 2007، ونُشِرت في نفس العام </span>
  <span id="freeText3078446801270003321" style="display:none">أحمد مراد.. <br />كاتب مصري من مواليد القاهرة 1978، تخرّج في مدرسة ليسيه الحرّية بباب اللوق عام 2006 قبل أن يلتحق بالمعهد العالي للسينما ليدرس التصوير السينمائي، وتخرّج عام 2001 بترتيب الأول على القسم، ونالت أفلام تخرّجه "الهائمون - الثلاث ورقات - وفي اليوم السابع" جوائز للأفلام القصيرة في مهرجانات بإنجلترا وفرنسا وأوكرانيا.. <br />بدأ أحمد كتابة روايته الأولي "فيرتيجو" في شتاء عام 2007، ونُشِرت في نفس العام عن دار "ميريت"، قبل أن تُترجم للّغة الإنجليزية عن دار "بلومزبيري"، ثم للإيطالية عن دار "مارسيليو"، والفرنسية عن دار "فلاماريون".. ثم تحولت الرواية لمسلسل تليفزيوني في رمضان من عام 2012.. <br />ثم أصدر أحمد روايته الثانية في فبراير 2010 بعنوان "تراب الماس" وتُرجمت للإيطالية عن دار "مارسيليو"، وأتبعها برواية "الفيل الأزرق" التي صدرت في أكتوبر من عام 2012.. </span>
